Topic: Math
Question: A company that makes wildlife videos purchases camera equipment for $\$ 32,400$. The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, after which it is considered to have no monetary value. How much is the camera equipment worth 4 years after it is purchased?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 10,800$
  B: $\$ 16,200$
  C: $\$ 21,600$
  D: $\$ 29,700$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years, which means its value decreases by the same amount every year.
  After 12 years, the equipment has no monetary value.
  Therefore, after 4 years, the equipment would have depreciated 1/3 of its total depreciation.
  To find this value, we have to subtract the depreciation amount from the original price of $\$ 32,400$.
  We can find the depreciation amount by dividing $\$32,400$ by the number of years the equipment depreciates.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Depreciation is when an asset loses value over time. Here, the camera equipment has a total lifespan of 12 years. So, the equipment loses an equal amount of value every year. 

Calculation:
After 4 years, the camera equipment would have lost a quarter of its total value.
The amount that the equipment has lost in value is $\$32,400/4=\$ 8,100$
The amount that the equipment is worth after 4 years is $\$ 32,400-\$ 8,100 = \$ 24,300$.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Since the camera depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, we can assume the depreciation is linear. 
  The total depreciation over 12 years would be  $\$ 32,400 - \$ 0 = \$ 32,400$.
  Therefore, the annual depreciation would be  $\frac{32400}{12}= \$ 2,700$.
  The value of the camera equipment 4 years after purchase will be  $ \$32,400 - (4 \times \$ 2,700) = \$ 21,600$. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate over 12 years.
  We can model the depreciation as a linear function that maps time to value.
  After 12 years, the value would have gone down to 0.
  For 4 years of depreciation, we need to find out the total depreciation and subtract it from the initial value.
  The depreciation per year is $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700 \text{ /year}$.
  Therefore, after 4 years of depreciation, the value is $\$32,400 - (\$2,700 \cdot 4 \text{ years})$.
Action: Answer("B")

In four years, $\frac{4}{12}$ or $\frac{1}{3}$ of the equipment's value depreciates.

Action: Answer("B")

Question: $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$In the equation above, if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: $c>1$
  B: $c=1$
  C: $c=-1$
  D: $c<-1$
Response 0:
Thought: 
We are given the equation $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$ where $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive.
Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, we know the numerator and denominator of the left side are negative and positive, respectively. 
Thus, their quotient must be negative. 
This tells us that $c$ must be negative. 
Since we cannot conclude anything else about $c$, our answer must be $c<0$.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
- If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is also negative.
- Since $a$ is negative, denominator $a$ is also negative. Hence, $\frac{a-b}{a}$ should be positive. Thus, $c$ should be a positive number.
- $c=1$ results in $a-b=a$. If $a$ is negative, then $a<b$. But given that $b$ is positive, this is not possible. Thus, $c=1$ is not possible.
-  If $c$ is negative, then $a-b$ is positive as this makes the numerator positive. But given that $a$ is negative, this cannot be possible. Thus, $c$ cannot be negative.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Since a is negative and b is positive, $a-b$ is always negative and $a$ is always less than $|b|$. Therefore, the fraction is always negative. 
  The value of $c$ depends on the values of $a$ and $b$.

  then $\frac{-2-1}{-2}=c \implies -\frac{3}{-2}=c \implies c=\frac{3}{2}>1$.
  Thus, we can safely eliminate options "B" and "C".
  If $c$ is positive, multiplying the left-hand side of the given equation by $-1$ will result in $c$ being negative.
  If $c$ is negative, multiplying the left-hand side of the given equation by $-1$ will result in $c$ being positive.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 5:
Thought:
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then the numerator: $a-b$ will be negative.
  However, the denominator: $a$ will also be negative. Therefore, $c$ can either be positive or negative.
  To determine the value of $c$, we can simplify the equation as follows:
$$\frac{a-b}{a}= 1 - \frac{b}{a} = c$$
  Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, we know that $|b| > |a|$, therefore $\frac{b}{a}>1$. 
  Thus, $1-\frac{b}{a}<0$. Therefore, to balance the equation, $c$ must be negative.

  So, if $c$ is negative, the right side $(1-c)$ will be positive, which implies that the denominator of the above equation is positive. Since $b$ is positive, $a$ will be negative.

Response 9:
Thought: 
We know that $a$ is negative, which means $|a|=-a$ and $a<0$. We also know that $b$ is positive, which means $b>0$. The given equation can be rewritten as $1-\frac{b}{a}=c$, which gives us $1 - \frac{b}{|a|} = c$. Since $|a|$ is positive, we can multiply both sides of the equation by $-1$ in order to flip the inequality signs. After rearranging, we get $\frac{b}{a}-1=-c$, which simplifies to $\frac{b-a}{a}=-c$. This means that $c$ is equal to the negative of the fraction $\frac{b-a}{a}$, which is always greater than $-1$.

  However, the denominator of the function will equal to $0$ when $x$ is equal to $1$ since it is in the denominator.
  So we need to check if $-1$ is the critical point.
  
Action: 
  We can use synthetic division to divide $(x^2-6x+3)$ by $(x-1)$.
  
           1  -7  10
      -1 | 1  -6  3
                3 -3
                -----
              1 -3  0

   So, $f(x) = \frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1} = x-3+\frac{0}{x-1} = x-3.$

   We can substitute $-1$ into the function for $x$ to get $f(-1)$.

Question: A cylindrical can containing pieces of fruit is filled to the top with syrup before being sealed. The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$. If $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ of syrup is needed to fill the can to the top, which of the following is closest to the total volume of the pieces of fruit in the can?
Choices:
  A: $7.5 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  B: $185 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The volume of the partially-filled cylindrical can is $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2} \cdot 10 \mathrm{~cm} = 750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of syrup needed to fill the remaining space is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}-110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} = 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  If the volume of the fruit is $x \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$, then the total volume of the fully-filled cylindrical can is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} + x \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The height and radius of the cylindrical can stay the same when syrup is added (or removed), so the radius and height of the section with fruit is also the same.
  Therefore, we can use ratios to set up and solve an equation for $x$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The syrup fills the entire cylindrical can, but the fruit only fills a portion of it. We need to solve for the volume of the interior of the can and then subtract the volume of syrup to get the volume of the fruit.
  The formula for the volume of a cylinder is $V=Bh$, where $B$ is the area of the base and $h$ is the height.
  We know that the area of the base is $75\mathrm{~cm}^{2}$ and the height is $10\mathrm{~cm}$. Therefore, the volume of the interior of the can is $V=75\mathrm{~cm}^{2} \times 10\mathrm{~cm}=750\mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the syrup is given as $110\mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  Therefore, the volume of the pieces of fruit is $750\mathrm{~cm}^{3}-110\mathrm{~cm}^{3}=640\mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

  Therefore, the volume occupied by fruit is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} = 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

Question: $$(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$The equation above is true for all $x$, where $a$ and $b$ are constants. What is the value of $a b$ ?
Choices:
  A: 18
  B: 20
  C: 24
  D: 40
Response 0:

  The equation is true for all values of x, so the coefficients of like terms on both sides of the equation must be equal. 
  The degree of the polynomial on the left-hand side is $(1+2)=3,$ and the degree of the polynomial on the right-hand side is $3 .$ 
  Equating the coefficients of $x^{3}$ on both sides, we get $20=a \cdot 5, a=4$
  Equating the coefficients of $x^{2}$ on both sides, we get $-9=15 a-b, b=15 a+9=75+9=84$
Action: $a b= 336$ So, Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:

Response 2:

  To find the value of $ab$, we need to simplify the given equation by multiplying it out, then compare the coefficient of the quadratic term $x^2$ with the standard quadratic form $ax^2+bx+c$.
  To get a quadratic term of $20x^3$, we need to multiply $(ax+3)$ with $5x^2$. So, $5a=20$ or $a=4$
  Multiplying out all the terms we get $20x^3-5bx^2+15x^2+12x-12=20x^3-9x^2-2x+12$. 
  Thus, $-5bx^2+15x^2=-9x^2$ or $b= -\frac{9}{-5}= \frac{9}{5}$

Action: Answer("A") 18. 

Solution: 
Multiplying out the left-hand side:
$$
\begin{aligned}(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)&=5 x^{2}a x+15 x^{2}+12 x-a bx^{2}-3 b x+4 a x-12b+12 \\ &=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12\end{aligned}
$$
Let's compare the coefficients of the polynomial in $x^3$:
$$
20=5a \ \ \Rightarrow \ \ a=4
$$
Let's compare the coefficients of the polynomial in $x^2$:
$$
0=-ab+15 \ \ \Rightarrow \ \ ab=15(4)=60
$$
Note that we don't need to check any other coefficients since there is only one possible equation involving $a$ and $b$ in this case. 
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A) }18}$.

Question: If $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$ and $a b=y$, which of the following is equivalent to $4 z+8 y$ ?
Choices:
  A: $(a+2 b)^{2}$
  B: $(2 a+2 b)^{2}$
  C: $(4 a+4 b)^{2}$
  D: $(4 a+8 b)^{2}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Notice that $4z+8y$ factors into $4(z+2y)$. 
  We can then substitute $z=a^{2}+b^{2}$ and $y=a b$.
  By doing so, we can simplify $4(z+2y)$ using some algebra. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
We can try to use the given equations to simplify each expression and see which one is equivalent to $4z+8y$.

$a^2+b^2 = z \implies 4z = 4(a^2+b^2) = (2a)^2 + 2(2ab)+(2b)^2 = (2a+2b)^2-8ab$

$ab = y \implies 8y = 8(ab) = 2(2ab) + 2(2ab) = 4ab + 4ab = 8ab$

$4z+8y = (2a+2b)^2 - 8ab + 8ab = (2a+2b)^2$

Action: Answer("B")

$4 z+8 y = (4)(a^{2}+b^{2}) + (8)(a b) = 4a^{2} + 8ab + 4b^{2} = 4(a^2 + 2ab + b^2) = 4(a+b)^{2}$
  
Action: Answer("B")

Then, $$
4 z+8 y=2(a^{2}+b^{2})+4 \cdot 2 a b=2(a+b)^{2}=(2 a+2 b)^{2}.
$$

  &= 4(a+b)^2 \\

  &= (2a+2b)^2
  \end{align*}

Question: Shipping Charges\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$\begin{array}{c}\text { Merchandise weight } \\ \text { (pounds) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Shipping } \\ \text { charge }\end{array}$ \\\hline5 & $\$ 16.94$ \\\hline10 & $\$ 21.89$ \\\hline20 & $\$ 31.79$ \\\hline40 & $\$ 51.59$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows shipping charges for an online retailer that sells sporting goods. There is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise. Which function can be used to determine the total shipping charge $f(x)$, in dollars, for an order with a merchandise weight of $x$ pounds?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=0.99 x$
  B: $f(x)=0.99 x+11.99$
  C: $f(x)=3.39 x$
  D: $f(x)=3.39 x+16.94$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The function is linear, which means it has the form of $f(x)=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The y-intercept in the context of the problem refers to the shipping charge when merchandise weight = 0, which is not given in the table.
  The slope can be determined from the table.
  The slope is the rate of change of the shipping charge per unit of weight, which can be computed using two data points in the table.
  To do that, we can pick the first and last rows of the table, and use the formula $m=\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$, where $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$ are the two data points.
  Let the first point be $(5,16.94)$ and the last point be $(40,51.59)$.
  Plugging in the values, we get $m=\frac{51.59-16.94}{40-5}=1.245$, which rounds to 1.25.
  Therefore, the function is $f(x)=1.25x+b$, where $b$ is the y-intercept.
  To solve for $b$, we can use one of the data points in the table.
  Let's use the first one: $16.94=1.25\cdot 5 + b$, which gives $b=10.19$.
  Therefore, the function is $f(x) = 1.25x+10.19$.

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $a$ & $3 a$ & $5 a$ \\\hline$y$ & 0 & $-a$ & $-2 a$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of $x$ and their corresponding values of $y$ are shown in the table above, where $a$ is a constant. If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, which of the following equations represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $x+2 y=a$
  B: $x+2 y=5 a$
  C: $2 x-y=-5 a$
  D: $2 x-y=7 a$
Response 0:
Thought:
There is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, the relationship is of the form $y=kx+b$. 
By comparing the second column "y" to the first column "x", we see that $k$ is negative. So, $k=-1$.
We substitute the first row values in the above equation:
$a = -1 \cdot a+b \Rightarrow b= 2a$
Thus, the equation is $y=-x+2a$.
We need to convert it to the form given in the choices to find the answer.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
 Since there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, we can assume that the equation of this relationship is of the form $y=kx+b$  where $k$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
 We then can choose two (different) values of $x$ and their corresponding values of $y$ to form a system of two equations. We can then solve for  $k$ and $b$.   
Action: We choose $x=a$ and $x=3a$ with their corresponding $y$ values $y=0$ and $y=-a$, respectively. 
 $$\begin{cases}0=ka+b\\ -a=3ka+b\end{cases}$$ 
 Substituting $b=-ka$ from the first equation into the second equation gives $-a=3ka-ka, \Rightarrow k= \frac{-a}{2a}=-\frac{1}{2}$. 
 Substituting $k= -\frac{1}{2}$ and $b=-ka=\frac{1}{2}a$ in $y=kx+b$, we get $y=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{1}{2}a$. Thus the answer is A: $x + 2y=a$.  Answer("A")

  Using point (5a,-2a) to solve for the y-intercept:
  $-2a=-\frac{1}{2}(5a)+b \implies b=-\frac{3}{2}a$
  The equation in slope-intercept form is $y=-\frac{1}{2}x-\frac{3}{2}a$. 
  Converting to standard form gives $2x-y=7a$.

In the experiment, 300 people were presented with a set of five pictures arranged in random order. Each person was asked to choose the most appealing picture. Of the first 150 participants, 36 chose the first picture in the set. Among the remaining 150 participants, $p$ people chose the first picture in the set. If more than $20 \%$ of all participants chose the first picture in the set, which of the following inequalities best describes the possible values of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: $p>0.20(300-36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  B: $p>0.20(300+36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  C: $p-36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
  D: $p+36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$

  Thus out of the total 300 participants, at most $\frac{36}{150}=\frac{12}{50}=\frac{6}{25}$ chose the first picture in the beginning.
  Since more than $20 \%$ participants choose the first picture in the set, we have:
  $\frac{p+36}{300}>0.2$
  so, $p>48$.
Action: Answer("D")

  So, the slope of the two lines that pass through the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ and also pass through the origin, must be the same.
  The slope of a line that passes through the two points $(x_1, y_1)$ and $(x_2, y_2)$ is given by $(y_2-y_1)/(x_2-x_1)$.
  If both slopes must be equal, then we can equate the two slopes and solve for $k$.
    $(32 - k)/(k - 2) = (k - 0)/(0 - 2)$.
    $(32 - k)/(k - 2) = - (k/2)$.
    $32 - k = -(k^2 - 2k)$
    $k^2 - (34)k + 32 = 0$
  We can use the quadratic formula to determine the value(s) of $k$ that solve the quadratic equation.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 6:
Thought:
    We're asked to compare the growth rates of a white birch and a pin oak tree, given that they start with diameters of 1 foot.
    From data outside of the problem, we know that different tree species grow at varying rates.
    We are supposed to calculate the (approximate) difference between the diameters of the two trees, 10 years from now.

Approach:
    According to the information given in the question, we could assume that both the trees will grow annually at similar constant rates.
    Then we can approximate the diameters 10 years later and calculate their difference.

Solution:
    Let us assume that the trees grow at a constant rate of `r` inches per year.
    According to formulas for the perimeter of the circle, the diameter of a circle is proportional to its circumference (perimeter). So, the increase in circumference of a circle is `2 * pi * r`, where `r` is the radius in inches.
    Let `D1` and `D2` be the diameters of white birch and pin oak trees respectively, we have:

    D1 = 12 inches (given)
    D2 = 12 inches (given)
    
    Since the trees grow at a constant rate of `r` inches per year, their diameter after `t` years can be approximated as:
    
    D1(t) = D1 + 2 * pi * r * t
    D2(t) = D2 + 2 * pi * r * t

    We want to find (D1(10) - D2(10)) which is approximately:

    (D1 + 2 * pi * r * 10) - (D2 + 2 * pi * r * 10)
    = D1 - D2 + 2 * pi * r * (-10)

    Since we are interested in the difference in inches, we convert the answer to inches.

    Let's suppose the difference is closest to `k` inches, we need to calculate `k`.

    D1 - D2 = 0 (since D1 = D2 = 12 inches)
    So, k = -20 * 2 * pi * r 
    (Note that `-20` comes out when the difference is subtracted as D1 - D2)

    We are now left with the task of calculating `r` to evaluate `k`.
    From published data in tree biology, Birch grows approximately `6 inches` per year and Pin oak grows approximately `15 inches` per year. Therefore the difference is about `9 inches` per year.

    r = 9/2pi (since the change in diameter is for 1 year)
    This is approximately equal to `1.43`.

    Now we can solve for `k`.
    k = -20 * 2 * pi * r
      = -20 * 2 * 3.14 * 1.43
      = -180.16
    Since the question asks for the absolute value of the difference, we can give the answer as `180`.

Which of the following equations gives the value, $v$, of the machine, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased for $0 \leq t \leq 10 ?$
Choices:
  A: $v=30,000-9,000 t$
  B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$
  C: $v=120,000+9,000 t$
  D: $v=120,000-30,000 t$
Response 0:
Thought: 
   The value of a machine depreciates by the same amount each year.
   The initial value of the machine is $120000$ and after $10$ years it will be $\$30,000$.
   We can use the slope-intercept form of a linear equation: $y = mx + b$ with $(x_1,y_1)=(0,120000)$ and $(x_2,y_2)=(10,30000)$ to solve for $v$
  
Calculation:
  We first calculate the slope $m$:
  \begin{align*}
  m &= \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1} \\
    &= \frac{30000 - 120000}{10 - 0} \\
    &= -9000
  \end{align*}
  Next, we substitute $m=-9000$, $b=120000$ and $v$ and $t$ in $y=mx+b$ and get:
  \begin{align*}
  v &= -9000t + 120000 \\
  v &= 120000-9000t \\
  \end{align*}

Topic: Math
Question: A cargo helicopter delivers only 100-pound packages and 120-pound packages. For each delivery trip, the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, and the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds. What is the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 5
  D: 6
Response 0:
Thought:
To maximize the number of 120-pound packages, we need to take advantage of the 10-package minimum and the maximum weight limit of 1,100 pounds.

Let:
  x: number of 100-pound packages
  y: number of 120-pound packages

We have two constraints:
  x + y >= 10 (minimum of 10 packages)
  100x + 120y <= 1100 (maximum weight of 1100 pounds)

We want to maximize y.

Action: Answer("C") -> 5
Explanation: 
  We can rewrite the first constraint as x >= 10 - y.
  Substituting x in the second constraint leads to:
  100(10-y) + 120y <= 1100
  1000 - 100y + 120y <= 1100
  20y <= 100
  y <= 5
  We cannot have a fractional number of packages, so the maximum number of 120-pound packages is 5, with the remaining 5 packages being 100-pound packages.
Response 1:
Thought:
  To maximize the number of 120-pound packages, the number of 100-pound packages needs to be minimized.
  Let x be the number of 120-pound packages and y be the number of 100-pound packages.

    x + y >= 10 (the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages)
    120x + 100y <= 1100 (the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds)
  Solving for y in the first inequality:
    y >= 10 - x
  Substituting y in the second inequality:
    120x + 100(10 - x) <= 1100
    20x <= 100
    x <= 5
  Since x needs to be a whole number, the maximum value of x is 5.

Action: Testing the answer choices.

  $f(2) =1$.
  Therefore, $x-2$ is not a factor of $f(x)$ because $2$ is not a root of $f(x)$.
  
Testing $x-3$:
  Let us find roots of $f(x)=0:$
  Interpolating between $x=2$ and $x=4$, we may hypothesize that $f(x)$ has a root near $x=3$, based on the fact that zero is encountered in the interval $[2,4]$.
  Similarly, interpolating between $x=4$ and $x=5$, we can hypothesize that $f(x)$ has a root near $x=4.5$ (we don't need to calculate the exact value).
  Therefore, $f(x)$ could be factored by $(x-3)^n$ for some integer $n$. We cannot conclude, however, that $x-3$ is a factor.

  $f(4) =0$.
  Therefore, $x-4$ is a factor of $f(x)$ because $4$ is a root of the $f(x)$.

Testing $x-5$:

  Therefore, $x-5$ is not a factor of $f(x)$ because $5$ is not a root of $f(x)$.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 7:
Thought:
We can use the Remainder Theorem to determine the factors.
If we divide $f(x)$ by a factor, the remainder will be zero when we use one of the given values of $x$.
We will attempt dividing $f(x)$ by the each of the given choices and check if the remainder is zero for one of the given values of $x$.
Action: 
  Notice that $f(2) = 1$, $f(4) = 0$, and $f(5) = -2$.
  \begin{align*}
    f(x)&=a(x-2)(x-b)(x-c) \\
    &=a(x^3 - (2b+c)x^2 + (2bc+2)d x -bcd)
  \end{align*}
  Let's start by testing choice A:
    When we divide $f(x)$ by $x-2$, the remainder is zero when $x=2$.
      $$f(x) = a(x-2)(x^2+bx+c)$$
      $$f(4) = a(4-2)(16+4b+c)=0 \quad \text{and} \quad f(5) = a(5-2)(25+5b+c)=0$$
      We can solve for b and c and we get:
      $$f(x) = 3(x-2)(x^2+5x+6)$$
    Therefore, $x-2$ is a factor of $f(x)$.
  Testing choice B:
    When we divide $f(x)$ by $x-3$, the remainder is zero for none of the given values of $x$.
      $$f(0) = a(0-2)(0-b)(0-c) = -3bc$$
    Since $-3bc \neq 0$ given these values of $f(x)$, $x-3$ cannot be a factor of $f(x)$.
  Testing choice C:
    When we divide $f(x)$ by $x-4$, the remainder is zero when $x=4$.
      $$f(x) = a(x-4)(x^2+wx+z)$$
      $$f(4) = a(4-4)(16+4w+z)=0$$
      $z=0$ and $w=-4$. Therefore, we get:
      $$f(x) = 3(x-4)(x^2-4x)$$
    Therefore, $x-4$ is a factor of $f(x)$.
  Testing choice D:
    When we divide $f(x)$ by $x-5$, the remainder is zero when $x=5$.
      $$f(x) = a(x-5)(x^2+mx+n)$$
      $$f(5) = a(5-5)(25+5m+n)=0$$
      $n=-5m-5$ so $f(x) = a(x-5)(x^2+mx-5m-5)$. 
      $$f(0)=a(-5)(5m-5)=15a$$
    Since $15a \neq 0$ given these values of $f(x)$, $x-5$ cannot be a factor of $f(x)$.
We have to select which one of the choices is a factor of $f(x)$. Thus, we eliminate (B) and (D) because they are not factors of $f(x)$.
Answer: Answer("A")

### Model: gpt-35-turbo | Prompt: concise | Exam: sat-math-100 | Problem 45 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the parabola with equation $y=(x-11)^{2}$ intersects the line with equation $y=25$ at two points, $A$ and $B$. What is the length of $\overline{A B}$ ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 12
  C: 14
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  Since we have $y=25$ intersects parabola equation $y=(x-11)^2$, 
  we know $(x-11)^2 = 25$, so we can solve for $x$. 
  Then, we can use the distance formula to find $AB$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
To find the two points $A$ and $B$, we need to solve the system of equations:
$\begin{cases}
y=25 \\
y = (x-11)^2
\end{cases}$

Then, the distance between $A$ and $B$ is $AB=|x_A-x_B|$.

Action: Answer("D") 16.

Solution:
Substituting $25$ for $y$ in the second equation, we get:
$25 = (x-11)^2$
Taking the square root of both sides, we get:
$5=x-11$ or $5=11-x$
Solving for $x$ in each equation, we get:
$x=16$ or $x=6$

Therefore, the two points at which the parabola intersects the line are $(16,25)$ and $(6,25)$. 

So $AB = |16 - 6| = 10$. 

Thus, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D) }16}$.
Response 2:
Thought:
  The standard form of a parabola is $y=a(x-p)^2+q$
  By setting $y=25$ and solving for $x$, we can find the $x$ coordinates of the points of intersection (A and B). 
  We can then compute the distance between these points using the distance formula. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought: 
- Based on information, one can see that the point B has the larger x-coordinate because y=25
- We know that $y = (x-11)^2$ and $y=25$ are the two equations for the parabola and line respectively
- Substituting $y = 25$ into $y = (x-11)^2$ gives us $(x-11)^2=25$, this simplifies to $x=6$ or $x=16$.
- Therefore, point A and B have coordinates $(6,25)$ and $(16,25)$, respectively.
- Using distance formula $AB = \sqrt{(16-6)^2+(25-25)^2} = \sqrt{100} = 10$
Action: Answer("A")

  To find the slope, we subtract y-coordinates then divide by the difference in x-coordinates.
  We then solve for the y-intercept.

Question: Dreams Recalled during One Week\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|c|c|}\hline& None & 1 to 4 & 5 or more & Total \\\hline\hlineGroup X & 15 & 28 & 57 & 100 \\\hlineGroup Y & 21 & 11 & 68 & 100 \\\hlineTotal & 36 & 39 & 125 & 200 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The data in the table above were produced by a sleep researcher studying the number of dreams people recall when asked to record their dreams for one week. Group X consisted of 100 people who observed early bedtimes, and Group Y consisted of 100 people who observed later bedtimes. If a person is chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream, what is the probability that the person belonged to Group Y ?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{68}{100}$
  B: $\frac{79}{100}$
  C: $\frac{79}{164}$
  D: $\frac{164}{200}$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  To calculate the probability, we need to divide the number of people who recalled at least 1 dream from Group Y by the total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream.
  Total number of people recalling at least 1 dream = 39 + 125 = 164.
  Number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream = 11 + 68 = 79.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream is 125+39 = 164. 
  This is our population.
  The total number of people from Group Y who remembered at least 1 dream is 11+68 = 79. 
  This is the number of successes.
  We can find the probability by dividing the number of successes by the population.
Action: Answer("C") $\frac{79}{164}$
Response 2:
Thought: 
Let A = event where a person recalled at least 1 dream
Let Y = event where a person is from Group Y
Use the formula P(Y|A) = P(Y and A) / P(A)
Find P(A) = the probability that a person recalled at least 1 dream = 164/200
Find P(Y and A) = the probability that a person is from Group Y and recalled at least 1 dream = 68/200
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  We need to find the probability of a person recalling at least one dream given that he/she belongs to Group Y.
  That is, P(Group Y | at least 1 dream).
  We can use Bayes' Theorem, P(A|B) = P(B|A) * P(A) / P(B).
  P(Group Y | at least 1 dream) = P(at least 1 dream | Group Y) * P(Group Y) / P(at least 1 dream).
  P(Group Y) = 100/200 = 1/2.
  P(at least 1 dream) = (39+125)/200 = 164/200.
  P(at least 1 dream | Group Y) = 68/100.
Action: Answer("C")

  Probability = $\frac{68}{164}$ = $\frac{17}{41}$
  
Action: Answer("C")

  Therefore, the probability of the person belonging to Group Y is $\frac{\frac{68}{164}}{\frac{164}{200}}= \frac{68}{100}$.

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& y<-x+a \\& y>x+b\end{aligned}$$In the $x y$-plane, if $(0,0)$ is a solution to the system of inequalities above, which of the following relationships between $a$ and $b$ must be true?
Choices:
  A: $a>b$
  B: $b>a$
  C: $|a|>|b|$
  D: $a=-b$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  If $(0,0)$ is a solution to the given system of inequalities, then the origin point $(0,0)$ satisfies both the inequalities.
  For $y<-x+a$, when $x=0$, we have $y<a$
  For $y>x+b$, when $x=0$, we have $y>b$
  Considering both together, we have $b < 0 < a$
  Therefore, $|a| > |b|$. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  We are given two inequalities:
  $$
  \begin{aligned}
   y<-x+a \\ 
   y>x+b
 \end{aligned}
 $$
 If $(0,0)$ satisfies both inequalities, we could plug in $x=0$ and $y=0$ and observe that $0<a$ and $0>b$. Therefore, the answer must be $A$ ($a>b$).
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  For point $(0,0)$ to be a solution to this system of linear inequalities,  $(0,0)$ must be below $y=-x+a$ and above $y=x+b$. 
  The slope of $y=-x+a$ is -1 and the slope of $y=x+b$ is 1, and both lines have y-intercepts greater than 0. 
  
  - Since $(0,0)$ lies below $y=-x+a$, $a$ must be greater than 0.
  - Since $(0,0)$ lies above $y=x+b$, $b$ must be negative.
Action: Answer("A")  
Response 3:
Thought:
  If $(0, 0)$ is a solution, we have: $0 < -0 + a$ and $0 > 0 + b$, which simplify to $0 < a$ and $0 > b$
Action: Answer("A")
Response 4:
Thought:
  If $(0, 0)$ is on the solution then we can just substitute in the point $(0,0)$ for $x$ and $y$ and solve for $a$ and $b$.
  The value of $a$ and $b$ should be opposite in sign, then the value that is greater in absolute value is the one that will dominate in the inequality.
  Hence, option B is the answer.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 5:
Thought: 
  To solve the system of inequalities above we can plot the boundary lines $y=-x+a$ and $y=x+b$. Then, depending on the values of $a$ and $b$ we will shade certain regions determined by the inequalities. If $(0,0)$ is a solution to the system, then point $(0,0)$ will be in one of the shaded regions of the plot. We need to analyze the equations of the boundary lines and the position of $(0,0)$ in the shaded region to determine the relationships between $a$ and $b$ that are true.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 6:
Thought: 
  Since $(0,0)$ satisfies both inequalities, we must have $0<-a$ and $0>b$. 
  Thus $a>0$ and $b<0$.
  Adding the two inequalities, we get $2y<a+b$, which implies $a+b>0$.
  To find the relation between $a$ and $b$, we consider when $x=1$ and $y=0$.
  In this case, the first inequality becomes $a-1<0$, or $a<1$.
  The second inequality is $b+1>0$, or $b>-1$.
  This means the minimum difference between $a$ and $b$ is $1$, and the possible scenarios are 
  $a=b+1$, $a=b+2$, $a=b+3$, and so on, with $a>1$ and $b<0$.
  Thus, the only correct choice is B: $b>a$. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 7:
Thought: 
  We want to find the relationship between $a$ and $b$.
  We plug in $(0, 0)$ for $(x, y)$ and simplify the system of inequalities to find the relationship between $a$ and $b$.
Action: 
  $$\begin{aligned}
  & y<-x+a \\
  & y>x+b \\
  \Rightarrow & 0<0+a \\
  & 0>0+b \\
  \Rightarrow & a>0 \\
  & b<0
  \end{aligned}$$
  Thus, the answer is (A) $a>b$.
Response 8:
Thought:
  For $(0,0)$ to be a solution, $0<-0+a$, i.e. $a>0$ and $0>0+b$, i.e. $b<0$.
  Thus we can add the inequalities vertically to cancel out $y$, which yields $0>a+b$. 
  From here we can eliminate two choices: neither $A$ nor $B$ is a possible answer.
  Since $a$ is positive and $b$ is negative, we have $|a|>-b$, and therefore $C$ is true.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 9:
Thought:
  Substitute $(0,0)$ into the system of inequalities to determine a relationship between $a$ and $b$.
  For $y<-x+a$ to hold when $(0,0)$ is a solution, $0<-0+a$ or $a>0$.
  For $y>x+b$ to hold when $(0,0)$ is a solution, $0>0+b$ or $b<0$.
  Therefore, $a>b$

Question: The weights, in pounds, for 15 horses in a stable were reported, and the mean, median, range, and standard deviation for the data were found. The horse with the lowest reported weight was found to actually weigh 10 pounds less than its reported weight. What value remains unchanged if the four values are reported using the corrected weight?
Choices:
  A: Mean
  B: Median
  C: Range
  D: Standard deviation
Response 0:
Thought:
  The mean, median, range, and standard deviation all represent properties of a dataset, and correcting the weight of one horse does not affect the other horses' data values.

Action: Answer("A") 

Therefore, the mean, which is the arithmetic average of the dataset, will remain unchanged if one horse's weight is corrected.
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The mean, median, range and standard deviation are all measures of central tendency or spread of the data.
  Subtracting 10 from a data point will only affect the mean and the median
  The range and the standard deviation won't be affected by just subtracting the same amount from a single value
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Mean, median, range, and standard deviation are statistical measures which summarize data.
  Correcting one weight value changes the range but does not affect the mean, median, and standard deviation values.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought:
  The "range" is the difference between the maximum and minimum values of a data set.
  The "mean" and "median" rely on the values of all the data set values.
  The "standard deviation" measures the variation of data in relation to the mean.
  Since only one data point (the lowest weight) is being subtracted, this won't change the "range".
  The change in the weight of only one horse won't have any effect on the "mean" nor the "standard deviation".
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 4:
Thought:
  The mean, median, range, and standard deviation are measurements of central tendency and dispersion in a set of data.
  Adding or subtracting a constant value from each data point in the set will not affect the range.
  The mean will change when we subtract a constant value from each data point.
  The median and the standard deviation may or may not change depending on where the lowest weight falls in the set.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 5:
Thought: 
  The mean, median, range, and standard deviation are measures of central tendency and data spread that do not necessarily consider outliers.
  Changing the weight of the horse with the lowest reported weight will only affect the range because it is based on the difference between the highest and lowest values in the data.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 6:
Thought:
  The mean, median, range and standard deviation are statistical measures calculated based on the given set of data. 
  Changing a single value in the data set affects some or all of these statistics.
  However, only one statistic is not affected by outliers or single data point changes - the median.
  Given that only one weight value was adjusted, it should only affect the mean and range.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 7:
Thought: 
When we add or subtract a constant from each data point, 
  the following values remain unchanged: 
    median
    quartiles (and therefore the interquartile range)
    percentiles
Standard deviation is sensitive to changes in the data, so it will change. 
Mean can be calculated using the sum of the observations, so when we change one observation, 
  we change the sum as well, result in changing the mean.
Range is affected by the maximum and minimum values, so it will change as well.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 8:
Thought: 
  The mean, median, range, and standard deviation are all calculations based on the weights of the horses in a stable. 
  Changing the weight of one horse will not affect the median, range, or standard deviation. 
  The mean, however, will change if a horse's weight is adjusted. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 9:
Thought:
  Changing the weight of one horse will change all four values except for one.
  The calculation for each value is as follows:
    - Mean: add all weights and divide by the number of horses.
    - Median: arrange the weights in order and find the middle value (or average of the two middle values for an even number of horses)
    - Range: subtract the smallest weight from the largest weight
    - Standard deviation: find the square root of the variance, where the variance is the sum of the squared differences between each weight and the mean, divided by the number of horses.
  The only calculation that will not be affected by a change in the weight of one horse is the range.
Action: Answer("C")

Question: Keith modeled the growth over several hundred years of a tree population by estimating the number of the trees' pollen grains per square centimeter that were deposited each year within layers of a lake's sediment. He estimated there were 310 pollen grains per square centimeter the first year the grains were deposited, with a $1 \%$ annual increase in the number of grains per square centimeter thereafter. Which of the following functions models $P(t)$, the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited?
Choices:
  A: $P(t)=310^{t}$
  B: $P(t)=310^{1.01 t}$
  C: $P(t)=310(0.99)^{t}$
  D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The growth is modeled by estimating the number of pollen grains per square centimeter deposited each year within layers of a lake's sediment.
  Keith estimated there were 310 pollen grains per square centimeter the first year the grains were deposited.
  Since there is a 1% increase in the number of grains per square centimeter thereafter, the model will include a factor of 1.01.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
To find the number of pollen grains deposited after several years, we can use the given initial value and constant annual increase in percentage. We can use an exponential function to model the population growth. The general form of an exponential function is $f(x)=ab^{x}$, where $a$ is the initial value and $b$ is the growth factor.
Action: Answer("D")

Thought:
  After the first year, there would be $310*1.01$ pollen grains per square centimeter.
  After two years, there would be $310*1.01*1.01$ pollen grains per square centimeter.
  The function should be $P(t) = 310(1.01)^t$. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  The tree population is growing by $1 \%$ annually. 
  We want to find a function that models $P(t)$ given information about the growth rate.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 4:
Thought: 
Keith estimated that $310$ pollen grains were deposited in the first year, and that number increased by $1 \%$ annually.
The function should multiply the pollen grains deposited in the first year by a rate greater than $1$ because there is positive growth annually.
Use answer choices to determine the base of the growth factor. 

Action: Answer("D")
Response 5:
Thought: 
  After each year, the growth is compounded by a factor of 1%.
  Thus, the pollen grain growth can be modeled by an exponential function.
  The function should start with 310 pollen grains ($t=0$).
  Option A does not account for yearly growth and is not exponential.
  Option C has a negative power, which represents decay, not growth.
Actions: 
  Option B: $P(t)=310^{1.01 t}$ - Incorrect. This option incorrectly compounds the rate of change by adding 1.01 to the exponent instead of multiplying.
  Option D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$ - Correct. This option correctly models the yearly growth by adding a factor of $(1+0.01)$ or 1.01, making it exponential. 
Answer: Answer("D")
Response 6:
Thought: 
  P(t) represents the number of pollen grains per square centimeter t years after the first year the grains were deposited. 
  The initial value of P(t) is 310 and the annual growth is $1\%$. 
  Exponential function equation would be y = ab^x, where a=310.
  Since the growth rate is $1\%$, the common ratio is 1+0.01 = 1.01. 
  Thus, the model would be P(t)= 310(1.01)^t.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 7:
Thought: 
  The initial number of the pollen grains is 310 and this number grows by $1 \%$ annually. We need to identify the function from the given choices that models this growth rate.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 8:
Thought:
  The number of pollen grains per square cm increases by 1% per year.
  The initial amount of pollen grains in the first year is 310.
  We want to find a function $P(t)$ that describes the pollen grain growth per year.
  Therefore, the correct formula is of the form $P(t)=310(1+r)^t$, where $r$ is the annual increase rate.
  We can solve for $r$ by noticing that after one year, the growth is given by $310(1+r)$, so $310(1+r)=310(1+\frac{1}{100})$, which implies $r=\frac{1}{100}$.
  Thus, the correct formula is $P(t)=310(1+\frac{1}{100})^t$
Action: Answer("D")

  After calculating both mean and standard deviation, we can compare them.

  B: $\$ 125$
  C: $\$ 150$
  D: $\$ 275$
Response 0:

  To figure out the difference between Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland's fees, we need to subtract the amount charged for Mr. Roland's job from that charged for Ms. Sanchez's job. 
  We can use the formula for C in this situation.
  Ms. Sanchez's electrician worked 2 hours longer on her job than Mr. Roland's. 
  Let's assign hours to these situations so that we can plug them into the equation.
  Let $h_1$ be the hours Mr. Roland's electrician spent on his job.
  Let $h_2=h_1+2$ be the hours Ms. Sanchez's electrician spent on her job.

$$
\begin{aligned}
\text{Ms. Sanchez's fee } - \text{ Mr. Roland's fee} & = C(h_2)-C(h_1) \\

& = (75h_1+150+125)-75h_1-125 \\
& = 150
\end{aligned}

Question: $$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$In the equation above, $k$ is a constant. If $x=9$, what is the value of $k$ ?

  A: 1
  B: 7
  C: 16
  D: 79

  We want to find the value of k.
  We can simply square both sides to isolate k and then solve for k.

Action: Answer("79")
 
We have, 
  $$\begin{aligned}\sqrt{k+2}-x&=0\\ \sqrt{k+2}&=x\\ \sqrt{k+2}&=9\\ k+2&=81\\ k &= 79\end{aligned}$$

Therefore, the answer is (D) 79.
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can solve for k if we substitute x with 9.
  Using algebra the equation can be re-written as: $\sqrt{k+2}=x$
  We know x=9, so we can use this to solve for k.
  First, square both sides of the equation to eliminate the square root. 
  
  $$\begin{aligned}
  \sqrt{k+2}&=9\\
  (\sqrt{k+2})^2&=9^2\\
  k+2&= 81 \\
  k&=79 \\
  \end{aligned}$$

$$a = -\frac{25+8x}{x^2}$$

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:

\[1.1l * (1 - \frac{p}{100})w = 0.88lw\]
Simplifying and solving for p:
\[110w - lw\frac{11p}{1000} = 0.88lw\]
\[22w = lw\frac{11p}{1000}\]
\[\frac{p}{100} = \frac{22}{11} * \frac{1}{10}\]
\[p = \boxed{\textbf{(C) }20}\]

Choices:
  A: 3 and 5
  B: 6 and 35
  C: 10 and 21
  D: 31 and 41
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Multiplying ($a x+2$) and ($b x+7$) gives quadratic polynomial in the form $A x^{2}+B x+14$
  $c$ will be the coefficient of x in this polynomial.
  We will need to find two combinations of $a$ and $b$ that gives the same polynomial.
Action: Answer("C") 
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to expand $(ax+2)(bx+7)$, equate its coefficients with $15x^2+cx+14$, and find the values of $c$ for which the relationship holds true.
  We can use the given fact that $a+b=8$.
  
Action: Expanding $(ax+2)(bx+7)$, we get:
  $(a x+2)(b x+7)=abx^2+7ax+2bx+14$
  
  Equating the coefficients of $x^2$ we get $ab=15$.
  
  Equating the coefficients of $x$ we get $7a+2b=c$.
  
  Since  $a+b=8$, we can rewrite the equation as $7a+2(8-a)=c$ and simplify to $c=6a+16$.
  
  We can substitute the first equation into the expression for c to obtain $c=6a+16=6(\frac{15}{b})+16=\frac{90+16b}{b}$.
  
  Thus, the two possible values of $c$ can be found by testing the different possible values of $b$ that divide $90+16b$.
  
  List the factors of 90 that are larger than 8 (since $b>0 \Rightarrow 16b > 8$ ).
  They are: 9,10,15,18,30,45,90
  
  Testing each of these factors, we see that only 10 and 21 are possible values for $c$.

Comparing coefficients of constant terms on both sides, we get $2 \times 7=14$.

Substituting a=3 and b=5, we get $c=7 \times 3+2 \times 5=29$.

Substituting a=5 and b=3, we get $c=7 \times 5+2 \times 3=37$.

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}\hline\multicolumn{3}{|c|}{Townsend Realty Group Investments} \\\hlineProperty address & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Purchase price } \\ \text { (dollars) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Monthly rental } \\ \text { price } \\ \text { (dollars) }\end{array}$ \\\hlineClearwater Lane & 128,000 & 950 \\\hlineDriftwood Drive & 176,000 & 1,310 \\\hlineEdgemont Street & 70,000 & 515 \\\hlineGlenview Street & 140,000 & 1,040 \\\hlineHamilton Circle & 450,000 & 3,365 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The Townsend Realty Group invested in the five different properties listed in the table above. The table shows the amount, in dollars, the company paid for each property and the corresponding monthly rental price, in dollars, the company charges for the property at each of the five locations. 23The relationship between the monthly rental price $r$, in dollars, and the property's purchase price $p$, in thousands of dollars, can be represented by a linear function. Which of the following functions represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $r(p)=2.5 p-870$
  B: $r(p)=5 p+165$
  C: $r(p)=6.5 p+440$
  D: $r(p)=7.5 p-10$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We want a linear function that represents the relationship between the monthly rental price and the property's purchase price.
  We need to determine the slope and the y-intercept of the line.
  The slope can be determined by calculating the change in y over the change in x.
  We can select two points from the table to calculate the slope and use the point-slope form of the equation to find the linear function.
Action: Answer("A").

Let's take two points from the table, Clearwater Lane (128,000, 950) and Driftwood Drive (176,000, 1,310).
The slope is (1310-950)/(176-128) = 360/48 = 7.5
The y-intercept can be found by using the point-slope form of the equation:
y - y1 = m(x - x1), where m is the slope, x1 and y1 are the coordinates of a point on the line.
Using the point (128, 950) and the slope 7.5, we have:
y - 950 = 7.5(x - 128)
y - 950 = 7.5x - 960
y = 7.5x - 10
We need to adjust the units for the purchase price, which is in thousands of dollars, so:
y = 7.5(p/1000) - 10
y = 2.5p - 870
Therefore, the linear function that represents the relationship between the monthly rental price and the property's purchase price is r(p) = 2.5p - 870.

  To form a linear function that represent the monthly rental price, we have to get the slope of the line that relates the monthly rental price with the purchase price. The formula for the slope is  $$m = \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}$$

The slope of the relationship line or the ratio of the change in the rental price to the change in the purchase price is the same as the slope between any two points on our line.

slope = $\dfrac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$ , where $(x_{1}, y_{1})$ and $(x_{2}, y_{2})$ are the coordinates of the two points.

The slope of the line is equal to the ratio between the increase in rental price to the increase in purchase price.
The rental price increased by $360$ dollars for an increase in the cost price of $48,000$ dollars. 
This simplifies to $3/400$. 

Now we have to find the y-intercept which is the value of y at which the line crosses the y-axis. 
To solve this, we can use one point, for example, $(176,000,1310)$. We have the slope already hence we can calculate the y-intercept as follows:
$y=m*x+c$
or $c=y-mp$
so, $c=1310 - \frac{3}{400}*176000 = 165$. 

Therefore, the linear function for the relationship between the monthly rental price $r$, and the property's purchase price $p$ is $r(p)=\dfrac{3}{400}p+165$.

Question: Roberto is an insurance agent who sells two types of policies: a $\$ 50,000$ policy and a $\$ 100,000$ policy. Last month, his goal was to sell at least 57 insurance policies. While he did not meet his goal, the total value of the policies he sold was over $\$ 3,000,000$. Which of the following systems of inequalities describes $x$, the possible number of $\$ 50,000$ policies, and $y$, the possible number of $\$ 100,000$ policies, that Roberto sold last month?
Choices:
  A: $x+y<57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y<3,000,000$
  B: $x+y>57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y>3,000,000$
  C: $x+y<57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y>3,000,000$
  D: $x+y>57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y<3,000,000$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let $a$ be the number of $50,000$ policies sold by Roberto, and let $b$ be the number of $\$100,000$ policies he sold last month.
  We are given two pieces of information:
   - $a + b < 57$: Roberto did not sell more than 57 policies.
   - $50,000a + 100,000b > 3,000,000$: the total value of policies sold was over $\$ 3,000,000$.
  It is easy to see that (A) cannot be true.
  We know that the $100,000$ policies contribute $100,000$ towards the total value of policies sold. Thus, if Roberto had sold $n$ $\$100,000$ policies, that is worth $100,000n$, and the $\$ 50,000$ policies need to contribute at least $3,000,000 - 100,000n$. For this value to have been contributed by fewer than $57 - n$ $\$50,000$ policies, we need $50,000(x) + 100,000(n)  \ge 3,000,000 - 100,000n$, where $x$ is the number of $\$50,000$ policies sold.
  Simplifying this gives $50,000x \ge 2,000,000 - 100,000n$, or equivalently, $x \ge 40 - 2n$. Then, combining this inequality with the fact that $x+y<57$, we obtain:
  $$
   \begin{cases}
    x \ge 40 - 2n\\
    x+y < 57
  \end{cases}
  $$
  Hence the answer is (C).

Based on the table, which of the following is closest to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never"?

  A: 0.31
  B: 0.38
  C: 0.45
  D: 0.69

  We want to find $P(\text{Answered "Always" } \mid \text{ Didn't answer "Never"})$
  This is a conditional probability, so we use the formula $P(A|B)=\frac{P(A\cap B)}{P(B)}.$
  Let $A=$ the event that the tablet user answered "Always" and let $B=$ the event that the tablet user did not answer "Never." 
  We need to find $P(A \mid B) = \frac{P(A\cap B)}{P(B)}.$
  We know from the table that $P(A\cap B) = 0.309$ and $P(B)= 1-P(\text{Answered "Never"}) = 1-0.313 = 0.687.$

  $$\text{P(Always and not Never)} = 30.9 \%$$

  Method 1: Elimination
  If we multiply the first equation by $2$ and the second equation by $3$, we can eliminate $y$ by adding the equations.
  By doing this we get: $3(2x-3y) - 2(3x-2y) = -6(-14) - (-2)(-6)$. Simplifying the left-hand side of this equation results in $-x$ = $6$, so $x=-6$. 
  Now if we substitute $x=-6$ into the second equation and solve for $y$, we get that $y=9$.

  Method 2: Substitution

$4y=-2x+6$
$y=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{3}{2}$
Comparing slopes, -1/2 is not the opposite reciprocal of 2/3.
Hence, this line is not perpendicular to the given line.

$6y=-2x+3$
$y=-\frac{1}{3}x+\frac{1}{2}$
Comparing slopes, -1/3 is not the opposite reciprocal of 2/3.
Hence, this line is not perpendicular to the given line.

Therefore, the equation that is perpendicular to the given equation is A. $3 x+2 y=6$

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$In the system of equations above, $k$ is a constant and $x$ and $y$ are variables. For what value of $k$ will the system of equations have no solution?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{12}{5}$
  B: $\frac{16}{7}$
  C: $-\frac{16}{7}$
  D: $-\frac{12}{5}$
Response 0:
Thought:
We can solve the system of equations using the elimination method and set it to something that is not true to create an equation for $k$.
$$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$
Multiplying the first equation by 4 and the second equation by $k$, we get:
$$\begin{aligned}& 4kx-12y=16\\& 4kx-5ky=7k\end{aligned}$$
If we subtract the first equation from the second equation above we get:
$$7k+12y=16$$
If $k=\frac{16}{7}$ then the system of equations will have no solution because the equations above produce a false statement.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can solve the systems of equations to determine the value of $k$ for which it has no solution. If there are no solutions to the system, then the equations are inconsistent, and the determinant of the 2x2 coefficient matrix is zero.
  The coefficients of the variable $x$ in the two equations of the system are the same. Thus we can find the value of $y$ by solving for $x$ in the first equation and substituting the resulting expression into the second equation to obtain an equation for $y$. 
  Setting the determinant of the coefficient matrix equal to zero will give the value of $k$ for which the system has no solution.

So we only need to find $k$ whose corresponding determinant of the coefficient matrix is zero.
The coefficient matrix is $\begin{pmatrix}k&-3\\4&-5\end{pmatrix}$.
The determinant is $k\times(-5)-(-3)\times4=-5k+12$.
The system of equations has no solution if the determinant is zero. So we need $-5k+12=0$ which implies $k=\frac{12}{5}$.

  A: $\frac{1}{8}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4}$
  C: 2
  D: 4
Response 0:
Thought: 
We can solve for $\frac{b}{a}$ by rearranging the given equation in terms of $\frac{b}{a}$ 
Action:  Answer("4")
Response 1:
Thought:
To solve for $\frac{b}{a}$, we need to isolate $\frac{b}{a}$ from the given equation. We will solve for $b$ first and then substitute into the fraction $\frac{b}{a}$.

Solution:
Starting with the given equation,
   $$ \frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2} $$
  Cross multiplying
  $$2a =\frac{b}{2}$$
Multiplying both sides by 2,
   $$4a = b$$
Substituting the value of $b$ in $\frac{b}{a}$ with $4a$, we have
   $$\frac{4a}{a} = 4$$
  Therefore, $\frac{b}{a} = 4$
